   <h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">
    List of mathematical symbols
   </h1>
   <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
    <div id="siteSub">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div>
    <div id="contentSub">
     <span class="mw-redirectedfrom">
      (Redirected from
      <a href="/w/index.php?title=Physics_symbols&amp;redirect=no" title="Physics symbols">
       Physics symbols
      </a>
      )
     </span>
    </div>
    <div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
     Jump to:
     <a href="#mw-head">
      navigation
     </a>
     ,
     <a href="#p-search">
      search
     </a>
    </div>
    <div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en">
     <dl>
      <dd>
       <div class="notice plainlinks">
        <i>
         This list is
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Lists#Incomplete_lists" title="Wikipedia:WikiProject Lists">
          incomplete
         </a>
         ; you can help by
         <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_mathematical_symbols&amp;action=edit">
          expanding it
         </a>
        </i>
        .
       </div>
      </dd>
     </dl>
     <p>
      This is a list of symbols found within all branches of
      <a href="/wiki/Mathematics" title="Mathematics">
       mathematics
      </a>
      to express a formula or to represent a
      <a href="/wiki/Constant_(mathematics)" title="Constant (mathematics)">
       constant
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      When reading the list, it is important to recognize that a mathematical concept is independent of the symbol chosen to represent it. For many of the symbols below, the symbol is usually synonymous with the corresponding concept (ultimately an arbitrary choice made as a result of the cumulative history of mathematics), but in some situations a different convention may be used. For example, depending on context, the
      <a href="/wiki/Triple_bar" title="Triple bar">
       triple bar
      </a>
      "
      <big>
       
      </big>
      " may represent congruence or a definition. Further, in mathematical logic, numerical equality is sometimes represented by "
      <big>
       
      </big>
      " instead of "=", with the latter representing equality of
      <a href="/wiki/Well-formed_formula" title="Well-formed formula">
       well-formed formulas
      </a>
      . In short, convention dictates the meaning.
     </p>
     <p>
      Each symbol is shown both in
      <a href="/wiki/HTML" title="HTML">
       HTML
      </a>
      , whose display depends on the browser's access to an appropriate font installed on the particular device, and in
      <a href="/wiki/TeX" title="TeX">
       TeX
      </a>
      , as an image.
     </p>
     <p>
     </p>

     <p>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Guide">
       Guide
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_mathematical_symbols&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Guide">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      This list is organized by symbol type and is intended to facilitate finding an unfamiliar symbol by its visual appearance. For a related list organized by mathematical topic, see
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_mathematical_symbols_by_subject" title="List of mathematical symbols by subject">
       List of mathematical symbols by subject
      </a>
      . That list also includes LaTeX and HTML markup and Unicode code points for each symbol.
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <b>
        Basic symbols:
       </b>
       Symbols widely used in mathematics, roughly through first-year calculus. More advanced meanings are included with some symbols listed here.
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        Symbols based on equality "=":
       </b>
       Symbols derived from or similar to the equal sign, including double-headed arrows. Not surprisingly these symbols are often associated with an
       <a href="/wiki/Equivalence_relation" title="Equivalence relation">
        equivalence relation
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        Symbols that point left or right:
       </b>
       Symbols, such as &lt; and &gt;, that appear to point to one side or another.
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        Brackets:
       </b>
       Symbols that are placed on either side of a variable or expression, such as |
       <i>
        x
       </i>
       |.
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        Other non-letter symbols:
       </b>
       Symbols that do not fall in any of the other categories.
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        Letter-based symbols:
       </b>
       Many mathematical symbols are based on, or closely resemble, a letter in some alphabet. This section includes such symbols, including symbols that resemble upside-down letters. Many letters have conventional meanings in various branches of mathematics and physics. These are not listed here. The
       <a href="#See_also">
        See also
       </a>
       section, below, has several lists of such usages.
       <ul>
        <li>
         <b>
          Letter modifiers:
         </b>
         Symbols that can be placed on or next to any letter to modify the letter's meaning.
        </li>
        <li>
         <b>
          Symbols based on
          <a href="/wiki/English_alphabet" title="English alphabet">
           Latin letters
          </a>
         </b>
         , including those symbols that resemble or contain an X
        </li>
        <li>
         <b>
          Symbols based on
          <a href="/wiki/Hebrew_alphabet" title="Hebrew alphabet">
           Hebrew
          </a>
          or
          <a href="/wiki/Greek_alphabet" title="Greek alphabet">
           Greek
          </a>
          letters
         </b>
         e.g.
         <big>
           ,, , , , , , , .
         </big>
         <i>
          Note:
         </i>
         symbols resembling  are grouped with "V" under Latin letters.
        </li>
       </ul>
      </li>
      <li>
       <b>
        Variations:
       </b>
       Usage in languages written right-to-left
      </li>
     </ul>

       <td align="center" bgcolor="#D0F0D0" rowspan="2">

          +
         </a>
        </div>
       </td>
       <td align="center" bgcolor="#FFFFFF" rowspan="2">
        <img alt="+ \!\," class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/5/b/a/5ba4c96940454c4d05519d2374d34bc0.png"/>
       </td>

        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:left;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         <a href="/wiki/Addition" title="Addition">

         </a>
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:center;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         <a href="/wiki/Plus_and_minus_signs" title="Plus and minus signs">
          plus
         </a>
         ;
         <br/>
         add
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:right;">
         <a href="/wiki/Arithmetic" title="Arithmetic">
          arithmetic
         </a>
        </div>
       </td>
       <td>
        4 + 6 means the sum of 4 and 6.
       </td>
       <td>
        2 + 7 = 9
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td style="padding:0px;">
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:left;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         <a href="/wiki/Disjoint_union" title="Disjoint union">
          disjoint union
         </a>
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:center;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         the disjoint union of ... and ...
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:right;">
         <a href="/wiki/Naive_set_theory" title="Naive set theory">
          set theory
         </a>
        </div>
       </td>
       <td>
        <i>
         A
        </i>
        <sub>
         1
        </sub>
        +
        <i>
         A
        </i>
        <sub>
         2
        </sub>
        means the disjoint union of sets
        <i>
         A
        </i>
        <sub>
         1
        </sub>
        and
        <i>
         A
        </i>
        <sub>
         2
        </sub>
        .
       </td>
       <td>
        <i>
         A
        </i>
        <sub>
         1
        </sub>
        = {3, 4, 5, 6} 
        <i>
         A
        </i>
        <sub>
         2
        </sub>
        = {7, 8, 9, 10} 
        <br/>
        <i>
         A
        </i>
        <sub>
         1
        </sub>
        +
        <i>
         A
        </i>
        <sub>
         2
        </sub>
        = {(3,1), (4,1), (5,1), (6,1), (7,2), (8,2), (9,2), (10,2)}
       </td>
      </tr>

       <td align="center" bgcolor="#D0F0D0" rowspan="3">

         </a>
        </div>
       </td>
       <td align="center" bgcolor="#FFFFFF" rowspan="3">
        <img alt="- \!\," class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/a/5/5/a55b5b5d9821f8e015830a817121d003.png"/>
       </td>
       <td style="padding:0px;">
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:left;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         <a href="/wiki/Subtraction" title="Subtraction">
          subtraction
         </a>
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:center;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         <a href="/wiki/Plus_and_minus_signs" title="Plus and minus signs">
          minus
         </a>
         ;
         <br/>
         take;
         <br/>
         subtract
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:right;">
         <a href="/wiki/Arithmetic" title="Arithmetic">
          arithmetic
         </a>
        </div>
       </td>
       <td>
        9  4 means the subtraction of 4 from 9.
       </td>
       <td>
        8  3 = 5
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td style="padding:0px;">
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:left;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         <a href="/wiki/Plus_and_minus_signs" title="Plus and minus signs">
          negative sign
         </a>
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:center;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         negative;
         <br/>
         minus;
         <br/>
         the opposite of
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:right;">
         <a href="/wiki/Arithmetic" title="Arithmetic">
          arithmetic
         </a>
        </div>
       </td>
       <td>
        3 means the
        <a href="/wiki/Negative_number" title="Negative number">
         negative
        </a>
        of the number 3.
       </td>
       <td>
        (5) = 5
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td style="padding:0px;">
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:left;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         <a href="/wiki/Complement_(set_theory)" title="Complement (set theory)">
          set-theoretic complement
         </a>
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:center;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         minus;
         <br/>
         without
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:right;">
         <a href="/wiki/Naive_set_theory" title="Naive set theory">
          set theory
         </a>
        </div>
       </td>
       <td>
        <i>
         A
        </i>
        
        <i>
         B
        </i>
        means the set that contains all the elements of
        <i>
         A
        </i>
        that are not in
        <i>
         B
        </i>
        .
        <br/>
        <br/>
        (
        <i>
         can also be used for set-theoretic complement as described below.
        </i>
        )
       </td>
       <td>
        {1,2,4}{1,3,4}= {2}
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td align="center" bgcolor="#D0F0D0" rowspan="2">
        <div class="nounderlines" style="font-size:200%;">
         <a href="/wiki/Plus-minus_sign" title="Plus-minus sign">
          
         </a>
        </div>

        <img alt="\int_a^b x^2 dx= \frac{b^3 - a^3}{3}" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/b/f/6/bf68c80f434c48574d7b95cd12135122.png"/>
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td style="padding:0px;">
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:left;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         <a href="/wiki/Line_integral" title="Line integral">
          line integral
         </a>
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:center;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         line/ path/ curve/ integral of ... along ...
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:right;">
         <a href="/wiki/Calculus" title="Calculus">
          calculus
         </a>
        </div>
       </td>
       <td>
        <span class="texhtml">
         <span style="position:relative; top:0.2em">
          <span style="font-style:italic; margin-right:0.3em;">
           <span class="Unicode">
            
           </span>
          </span>
          <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.2em;font-size:85%;text-align:left">
           <br/>
           <i>
            C
           </i>
          </span>
         </span>
         <i>
          f
         </i>
         d
         <i>
          s
         </i>
        </span>
        means the integral of
        <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">
         f
        </span>
        along the curve
        <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">
         C
        </span>
        ,
        <img alt="\int_a^b f(\mathbf{r}(t)) |\mathbf{r}'(t)|\, dt" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/9/0/d/90d60573cd5ca583643e0b248dee60f5.png"/>
        , where
        <span class="texhtml">
         <b>
          r
         </b>
        </span>
        is a parametrization of
        <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">
         C
        </span>
        . (If the curve is closed, the symbol
        <span style="position:relative; top:0.2em">
         <span style="font-style:italic; margin-right:0.3em;">
          <span class="Unicode">
           
          </span>
         </span>
         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.2em;font-size:85%;text-align:left">
          <br/>
         </span>
        </span>
        may be used instead, as described below.)
       </td>
       <td>
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td align="center" bgcolor="#D0F0D0" rowspan="1">
        <div class="nounderlines" style="font-size:200%;">
         <span style="position:relative; top:0.2em">
          <span style="font-style:italic; margin-right:0.3em;">
           <span class="Unicode">
            
           </span>
          </span>
          <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.2em;font-size:85%;text-align:left">
           <br/>
          </span>
         </span>
        </div>
       </td>
       <td align="center" bgcolor="#FFFFFF" rowspan="1">
        <img alt="\oint \!\," class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/c/2/1/c21b388a48eea039c6761e4bac9e5bb4.png"/>
       </td>
       <td style="padding:0px;">
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:left;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         Contour integral;
         <br/>
         closed
         <a href="/wiki/Line_integral" title="Line integral">
          line integral
         </a>
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:center;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         contour integral of
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:right;">
         <a href="/wiki/Calculus" title="Calculus">
          calculus
         </a>
        </div>
       </td>
       <td>
        Similar to the integral, but used to denote a single integration over a closed curve or loop. It is sometimes used in physics texts involving equations regarding
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gauss%27s_Law" title="Gauss's Law">
         Gauss's Law
        </a>
        , and while these formulas involve a closed
        <a href="/wiki/Surface_integral" title="Surface integral">
         surface integral
        </a>
        , the representations describe only the first integration of the volume over the enclosing surface. Instances where the latter requires simultaneous double integration, the symbol
        <span style="position:relative; top:0.2em">
         <span style="font-style:italic; margin-right:0.3em;">
          <span class="Unicode">
           
          </span>
         </span>
         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.2em;font-size:85%;text-align:left">
          <br/>
         </span>
        </span>
        would be more appropriate. A third related symbol is the closed
        <a href="/wiki/Volume_integral" title="Volume integral">
         volume integral
        </a>
        , denoted by the symbol
        <span style="position:relative; top:0.2em">
         <span style="font-style:italic; margin-right:0.3em;">
          <span class="Unicode">
           
          </span>
         </span>
         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.2em;font-size:85%;text-align:left">
          <br/>
         </span>
        </span>
        .
        <p>
         The contour integral can also frequently be found with a subscript capital letter C,
         <span class="texhtml">
          <span style="position:relative; top:0.2em">
           <span style="font-style:italic; margin-right:0.3em;">
            <span class="Unicode">
             
            </span>
           </span>
           <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.2em;font-size:85%;text-align:left">
            <br/>
           </span>
          </span>
          <sub>
           <i>
            C
           </i>
          </sub>
         </span>
         , denoting that a closed loop integral is, in fact, around a contour
         <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">
          C
         </span>
         , or sometimes dually appropriately, a circle
         <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">
          C
         </span>
         . In representations of Gauss's Law, a subscript capital S,
         <span class="texhtml">
          <span style="position:relative; top:0.2em">
           <span style="font-style:italic; margin-right:0.3em;">
            <span class="Unicode">
             
            </span>
           </span>
           <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.2em;font-size:85%;text-align:left">
            <br/>
           </span>
          </span>
          <sub>
           <i>
            S
           </i>
          </sub>
         </span>
         , is used to denote that the integration is over a closed surface.
        </p>
       </td>
       <td>
        If
        <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">
         C
        </span>
        is a
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jordan_curve" title="Jordan curve">
         Jordan curve
        </a>
        about 0, then
        <img alt="\oint_C {1 \over z}\,dz = 2\pi i" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/e/5/a/e5a1f7a5d04878c5db1c1a9fd56f1d4f.png"/>
        .
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td align="center" bgcolor="#D0F0D0" rowspan="1">
        <div class="nounderlines" style="font-size:200%;">
         <a href="/wiki/Therefore_sign" title="Therefore sign">
          
         </a>
        </div>
       </td>
       <td align="center" bgcolor="#FFFFFF" rowspan="1">
        <img alt="\therefore \!\," class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/c/5/3/c53f2396d00752c26ed1b95d75e02659.png"/>
       </td>
       <td style="padding:0px;">
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:left;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Therefore" title="Therefore">
          therefore
         </a>
        </div>

         therefore;
         <br/>
         so;
         <br/>
         hence
        </div>

         everywhere
        </div>
       </td>
       <td>
        Sometimes used in proofs before
        <a href="/wiki/Logical_consequence" title="Logical consequence">
         logical consequences
        </a>
        .
       </td>
       <td>
        All humans are mortal. Socrates is a human.  Socrates is mortal.
       </td>

         </a>

       </td>

        <img alt="\because \!\," class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/0/a/b/0ab277d305236c1f5274035ba1309cba.png"/>
       </td>
       <td style="padding:0px;">
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:left;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         <a class="extiw" href="//en.wiktionary.org/wiki/because" title="wiktionary:because">
          because

         <br/>
         since
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:right;">
         everywhere
        </div>
       </td>
       <td>
        Sometimes used in proofs before reasoning.
       </td>
       <td>
        11 is
        <a href="/wiki/Prime_number" title="Prime number">
         prime
        </a>
         it has no positive integer factors other than itself and one.
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td align="center" bgcolor="#D0F0D0" rowspan="2">
        <div class="nounderlines" style="font-size:200%;">
         <a href="/wiki/Exclamation_mark" title="Exclamation mark">
          !
         </a>
        </div>
       </td>
       <td align="center" bgcolor="#FFFFFF" rowspan="2">
        <img alt="! \!\," class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/6/4/e/64e0cba39b75ec61a990d476bf338d10.png"/>
       </td>
       <td style="padding:0px;">
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:left;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         <a href="/wiki/Factorial" title="Factorial">
          factorial
         </a>
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:center;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         factorial
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:right;">
         <a href="/wiki/Combinatorics" title="Combinatorics">
          combinatorics
         </a>
        </div>
       </td>
       <td>
        <i>
         n
        </i>
        ! means the product 1  2  ... 
        <i>
         n
        </i>
        .
       </td>
       <td>
        <img alt="4! = 1\times2\times3\times4 = 24" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/a/7/8/a785ebe436b48001486c1c720581f0ef.png"/>
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td style="padding:0px;">
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:left;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Logical_negation" title="Logical negation">
          logical negation
         </a>
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:center;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         not
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:right;">
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Propositional_logic" title="Propositional logic">
          propositional logic
         </a>
        </div>
       </td>
       <td>
        The statement!
        <i>
         A
        </i>
        is true if and only if
        <i>
         A
        </i>
        is false.
        <br/>
        <br/>
        A slash placed through another operator is the same as "!" placed in front.
        <br/>
        <br/>
        (
        <i>
         The symbol
        </i>
        !
        <i>
         is primarily from computer science. It is avoided in mathematical texts, where the notation
        </i>
        
        <i>
         A
        </i>
        <i>
         is preferred.
        </i>
        )
       </td>
       <td>
        !(!
        <i>
         A
        </i>
        )
        <i>
         A
        </i>
        <br/>
        <i>
         x
        </i>
        
        <i>
         y
        </i>
        !(
        <i>
         x
        </i>
        =
        <i>
         y
        </i>
        )
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td align="center" bgcolor="#D0F0D0" rowspan="1">
        <div class="nounderlines" style="font-size:200%;">
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Not_sign" title="Not sign">
          
         </a>
         <br/>
         <br/>
         
        </div>
       </td>
       <td align="center" bgcolor="#FFFFFF" rowspan="1">
        <img alt="\neg \!\," class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/0/2/3/023b800a1806490ff857cf9d69a260df.png"/>
        <br/>
        <br/>
        <img alt="\sim \!\," class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/9/e/e/9eeb35ca4391514c3e5317750ce68e16.png"/>
       </td>
       <td style="padding:0px;">
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:left;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Logical_negation" title="Logical negation">
          logical negation
         </a>
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:center;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         not
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:right;">
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Propositional_logic" title="Propositional logic">
          propositional logic
         </a>
        </div>
       </td>
       <td>
        The statement 
        <i>
         A
        </i>
        is true if and only if
        <i>
         A
        </i>
        is false.
        <br/>
        <br/>
        A slash placed through another operator is the same as "" placed in front.
        <br/>
        <br/>
        (
        <i>
         The symbol
        </i>
        ~
        <i>
         has many other uses, so
        </i>
        
        <i>
         or the slash notation is preferred. Computer scientists will often use
        </i>
        !
        <i>
         but this is avoided in mathematical texts.
        </i>
        )
       </td>
       <td>
        (
        <i>
         A
        </i>
        )
        <i>
         A
        </i>
        <br/>
        <i>
         x
        </i>
        
        <i>
         y
        </i>
         (
        <i>
         x
        </i>
        =
        <i>
         y
        </i>
        )
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td align="center" bgcolor="#D0F0D0" rowspan="1">
        <div class="nounderlines" style="font-size:200%;">
         <a href="/wiki/Proportionality_(mathematics)" title="Proportionality (mathematics)">
          
         </a>
        </div>
       </td>
       <td align="center" bgcolor="#FFFFFF" rowspan="1">
        <img alt="\propto \!\," class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/0/2/b/02b6d397e015e480420f59701c1a1d26.png"/>
       </td>
       <td style="padding:0px;">
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:left;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         <a href="/wiki/Proportionality_(mathematics)" title="Proportionality (mathematics)">
          proportionality
         </a>
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:center;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         is proportional to;
         <br/>
         varies as
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:right;">
         everywhere
        </div>
       </td>
       <td>
        <i>
         y
        </i>
        
        <i>
         x
        </i>
        means that
        <i>
         y
        </i>
        =
        <i>
         kx
        </i>
        for some constant
        <i>

        </i>
        .
       </td>
       <td>
        if
        <i>
         y
        </i>
        = 2
        <i>
         x
        </i>
        , then
        <i>
         y
        </i>
        
        <i>
         x
        </i>
        .
       </td>

       </td>

      <tr>
       <td align="center" bgcolor="#D0F0D0" rowspan="1">

       </td>

        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:left;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">

      <tr>
       <td align="center" bgcolor="#D0F0D0" rowspan="1">
        <div class="nounderlines" style="font-size:200%;">
         <a href="/wiki/Equals_sign" title="Equals sign">
          =
         </a>
        </div>
       </td>
       <td align="center" bgcolor="#FFFFFF" rowspan="1">
        <img alt="=" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/4/3/e/43ec3e5dee6e706af7766fffea512721.png"/>
       </td>
       <td style="padding:0px;">
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:left;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">

         </a>
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:center;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         is equal to;
         <br/>
         equals
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:right;">

       <td>
        <img alt="x = y" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/9/1/9/919860b52317a584e5de6f3257631d16.png"/>
        means
        <img alt="x" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/9/d/d/9dd4e461268c8034f5c8564e155c67a6.png"/>
        and
        <img alt="y" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/4/1/5/415290769594460e2e485922904f345d.png"/>
        represent the same math object (Both symbols have the same value).
       </td>
       <td>
        <img alt="2 = 2" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/a/0/8/a08af937649cb606cb4b1c27efecd4c5.png"/>
        <br/>
        <img alt="1 + 1 = 2" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/0/c/f/0cfae383362bc63d7ac429a5755fef05.png"/>
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td align="center" bgcolor="#D0F0D0" rowspan="1">
        <div class="nounderlines" style="font-size:200%;">
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Not_equals_sign" title="Not equals sign">
          
         </a>
        </div>
       </td>
       <td align="center" bgcolor="#FFFFFF" rowspan="1">
        <img alt="\ne" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/b/d/0/bd0d5f08997b7a4ad8598963f7e50231.png"/>
       </td>
       <td style="padding:0px;">
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:left;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         <a href="/wiki/Inequality_(mathematics)" title="Inequality (mathematics)">
          inequality
         </a>
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:center;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         is not equal to;
         <br/>
         does not equal
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:right;">
         everywhere
        </div>
       </td>
       <td>
        <img alt="x \ne y" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/7/3/c/73c7070fbc887c38daea22738774c01c.png"/>
        means that
        <img alt="x" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/9/d/d/9dd4e461268c8034f5c8564e155c67a6.png"/>
        and
        <img alt="y" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/4/1/5/415290769594460e2e485922904f345d.png"/>
        do not represent the same math object (Both symbols do not have the same value).
        <br/>
        <br/>
        (
        <i>
         The forms
        </i>
        !=, /=
        <i>
         or
        </i>
        &lt;&gt;
        <i>
         are generally used in programming languages where ease of typing and use of
         <a href="/wiki/ASCII" title="ASCII">
          ASCII
         </a>
         text is preferred.
        </i>
        )
       </td>
       <td>
        <img alt="2 + 2 \ne 5" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/3/4/c/34c7c6cc9056e9661c9e6776de39751b.png"/>
       </td>

         <br/>

        </div>

       <td>

        </div>

       <td align="center" bgcolor="#FFFFFF" rowspan="1">
        <img alt="\Leftrightarrow " class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/0/1/4/014cced2b73c22eb88cdc6901afb0c9d.png"/>
        <br/>

        <img alt="\leftrightarrow " class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/1/b/1/1b18a4c4fc578ef4cfd1cc0eb0daa473.png"/>
       </td>
       <td style="padding:0px;">
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:left;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Material_equivalence" title="Material equivalence">
          material equivalence
         </a>
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:center;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         if and only if;
         <br/>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iff" title="Iff">
          iff
         </a>
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:right;">
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Propositional_logic" title="Propositional logic">
          propositional logic
         </a>
        </div>
       </td>
       <td>
        <i>
         A
        </i>
        
        <i>
         B
        </i>
        means
        <i>
         A
        </i>
        is true if
        <i>
         B
        </i>
        is true and
        <i>
         A
        </i>
        is false if
        <i>
         B
        </i>
        is false.
       </td>
       <td>
        <i>
         x
        </i>
        + 5=
        <i>
         y
        </i>
        + 2
        <i>
         x
        </i>
        + 3=
        <i>
         y
        </i>
       </td>
      </tr>

        <i>
         y
        </i>

        <dl>

      <tr>
       <td style="padding:0px;">
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:left;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         <a href="/wiki/Inequality_(mathematics)#Vector_inequalities" title="Inequality (mathematics)">
          vector inequality
         </a>
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:center;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         ... is less than or equal... is greater than or equal...
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:right;">
         <a href="/wiki/Order_theory" title="Order theory">
          order theory
         </a>
        </div>
       </td>
       <td>
        <i>
         x
        </i>
        
        <i>
         y
        </i>
        means that each component of vector
        <i>
         x
        </i>
        is less than or equal to each corresponding component of vector
        <i>
         y
        </i>
        .
        <br/>
        <br/>
        <i>
         x
        </i>
        
        <i>
         y
        </i>
        means that each component of vector
        <i>
         x
        </i>
        is greater than or equal to each corresponding component of vector
        <i>
         y
        </i>
        .
        <br/>
        <br/>
        <i>
         It is important to note that
        </i>
        x
        <i>
         
        </i>
        y
        <i>
         remains true if every element is equal. However, if the operator is changed,
        </i>
        x
        <i>
         
        </i>
        y
        <i>
         is true if and only if
        </i>
        x
        <i>
         
        </i>
        y
        <i>
         is also true.
        </i>
       </td>
       <td>
       </td>

          </span>

          material implication
         </a>
        </div>

         implies;
         <br/>
         if ... then
        </div>

        <i>
         A
        </i>
        
        <i>
         B
        </i>

        </i>

        <i>
         B
        </i>
        is also true; if
        <i>
         A
        </i>
        is false then nothing is said about
        <i>
         B
        </i>
        .
        <br/>
        <br/>
        (
        <i>
         may mean the same as
        </i>
        
        <i>
         , or it may have the meaning for
         <a href="/wiki/Function_(mathematics)" title="Function (mathematics)">
          functions
         </a>
         given below.
        </i>
        )
        <br/>
        <br/>
        (
        <i>
         may mean the same as
        </i>
        
        <i>

         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Copi_4-0">

           <span>
            [
           </span>
           4
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
         or it may have the meaning for
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Superset" title="Superset">
          superset
         </a>
         given below.
        </i>

       </td>
       <td>
        <i>
         x
        </i>
        = 2
        <i>
         x
        </i>
        <sup>
         2
        </sup>
        = 4 is true, but
        <i>
         x
        </i>

        </sup>

         x
        </i>

        <i>

        <img alt="{\ \choose\ }" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/c/1/f/c1f29df58b64312588b971b21d0a41af.png"/>
       </td>
       <td style="padding:0px;">
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:left;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">

         </a>
         ;
         <br/>
         <a href="/wiki/Binomial_coefficient" title="Binomial coefficient">

         </a>
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:center;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         <i>
          n
         </i>
         choose
         <i>
          k
         </i>
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:right;">
         <a href="/wiki/Combinatorics" title="Combinatorics">
          combinatorics
         </a>
        </div>
       </td>
       <td>
        <img alt="\begin{pmatrix} n \\ k \end{pmatrix}
=\frac{n!/(n-k)!}{k!}
= \frac{(n-k+1)\cdots(n-2)\cdot(n-1)\cdot n}{k!}
" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/8/3/a/83ac75be63619e04c191b40b0698b164.png"/>
        <br/>
        means (in the case of
        <i>
         n
        </i>
        = positive integer) the number of combinations of
        <i>
         k
        </i>
        elements drawn from a set of
        <i>
         n
        </i>
        elements.
        <br/>
        <br/>
        (
        <i>
         This may also be written as
        </i>
        C(
        <i>
         n
        </i>

         k
        </i>

        <i>
         n
        </i>
        ;
        <i>
         k
        </i>
        ),
        <sub>
         <i>
          n
         </i>
        </sub>
        <i>
         C
        </i>
        <sub>
         <i>
          k
         </i>
        </sub>
        ,
        <sup>
         <i>
          n
         </i>
        </sup>
        <b>
         C
        </b>
        <sub>
         <i>
          k
         </i>
        </sub>
        , or
        <img alt="\left\langle\begin{matrix} n \\ k \end{matrix}\right\rangle" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/f/3/4/f342651dc62a836ae04dac8c94206c8e.png"/>
        .)
       </td>
       <td>

        <br/>

         <img alt="

        Let
        <i>
         a
        </i>
        ~
        <i>

        </i>

        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iff" title="Iff">

        </i>
        
        <i>

        </a>
        5).

        </i>

        </i>

        <i>

        </i>
        to 0.

       <td>
        An ordered list (or sequence, or horizontal vector, or row vector) of values.
        <p>
         (
         <i>
          Note that the notation
         </i>
         (
         <i>
          a
         </i>
         ,
         <i>
          b
         </i>
         )
         <i>
          is ambiguous: it could be an ordered pair or an open interval. Set theorists and computer scientists often use angle brackets
         </i>
         
         <i>
          instead of parentheses.
         </i>
         )
        </p>
       </td>
       <td>
        (
        <i>
         a
        </i>
        ,
        <i>
         b
        </i>
        ) is an ordered pair (or 2-tuple).
        <p>
         (
         <i>
          a
         </i>
         ,
         <i>
          b
         </i>
         ,
         <i>
          c
         </i>
         ) is an ordered triple (or 3-tuple).
        </p>
        <p>
         ( ) is the
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Empty_tuple" title="Empty tuple">
          empty tuple
         </a>
         (or 0-tuple).
        </p>
       </td>
      </tr>

       <td style="padding:0px;">
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:left;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inner_product" title="Inner product">
          inner product
         </a>
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:center;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         inner product of
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:right;">
         <a href="/wiki/Linear_algebra" title="Linear algebra">
          linear algebra
         </a>
        </div>
       </td>
       <td>
        
        <i>
         u
        </i>
        ,
        <i>
         v
        </i>
         means the inner product of
        <i>
         u
        </i>
        and
        <i>
         v
        </i>
        , where
        <i>
         u
        </i>
        and
        <i>
         v
        </i>
        are members of an
        <a href="/wiki/Inner_product_space" title="Inner product space">
         inner product space
        </a>
        .
        <br/>
        <br/>
        <i>
         Note that the notation
        </i>
        
        <i>
         u
        </i>
        ,
        <i>
         v
        </i>
        
        <i>
         may be ambiguous: it could mean the inner product or the
         <a href="/wiki/Linear_span" title="Linear span">
          linear span
         </a>
         .
        </i>
        <br/>
        <br/>
        <i>
         There are many variants of the notation, such as
        </i>
        
        <i>
         u
        </i>
        |
        <i>
         v
        </i>
        
        <i>
         and
        </i>
        (
        <i>
         u
        </i>
        |
        <i>
         v
        </i>
        ),
        <i>
         which are described below. For spatial vectors, the
         <a href="/wiki/Dot_product" title="Dot product">
          dot product
         </a>
         notation
        </i>
        ,
        <i>
         x
        </i>
        
        <i>
         y
        </i>
        <i>
         is common. For matrices, the colon notation
        </i>
        <i>
         A
        </i>
        :
        <i>
         B
        </i>
        <i>
         may be used. As
        </i>
        
        <i>
         and
        </i>
        
        <i>
         can be hard to type, the more "keyboard friendly" forms
        </i>
        &lt;
        <i>
         and
        </i>
        &gt;
        <i>
         are sometimes seen. These are avoided in mathematical texts.
        </i>
       </td>
       <td>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Dot_product" title="Dot product">
         standard inner product
        </a>
        between two vectors
        <i>
         x
        </i>
        =(2,3) and
        <i>
         y
        </i>
        =(1,5) is:
        <br/>
        x,y=21+35= 13
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td style="padding:0px;">
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:left;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         average
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:center;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">

        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:right;">
         <a href="/wiki/Statistics" title="Statistics">
          statistics
         </a>

       </td>
       <td>
        let S be a subset of N for example,
        <img alt=" \langle S \rangle " class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/0/0/c/00c1dc37c488f3467d76cdd967cede4b.png"/>
        represents the average of all the element in S.
       </td>
       <td>
        for a time series:
        <i>
         g
        </i>
        (
        <i>
         t
        </i>
        ) (
        <i>
         t
        </i>
        = 1, 2,...)
        <p>
         we can define the
         <a href="/wiki/Algebraic_structure" title="Algebraic structure">
          structure
         </a>
         functions
         <i>
          S
          <sub>
           q
          </sub>
         </i>
         (

         ):
        </p>
        <dl>
         <dd>
          <img alt="S_q = \langle |g(t + \tau) - g(t)|^q  \rangle_t " class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/2/9/5/295ff4f151f1e60a87662771f9813df5.png"/>
         </dd>
        </dl>
       </td>

      <tr>
       <td style="padding:0px;">
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:left;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         <a href="/wiki/Linear_span" title="Linear span">
          linear span
         </a>
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:center;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">

       <td>
        
        <i>
         S
        </i>
         means the span of
        <i>
         S
        </i>
        
        <i>
         V
        </i>
        . That is, it is the intersection of all subspaces of
        <i>
         V
        </i>
        which contain
        <i>
         S
        </i>
        .
        <br/>
        
        <i>
         u
        </i>
        <sub>
         1
        </sub>
        ,
        <i>
         u
        </i>
        <sub>
         2
        </sub>

        <i>
         u
        </i>
        <sub>
         1
        </sub>
        ,
        <i>
         u
        </i>
        <sub>
         2
        </sub>
        ,...}.
        <br/>
        <p>
         <br/>
         <i>
          Note that the notation
         </i>
         
         <i>
          u
         </i>
         ,
         <i>
          v
         </i>
         
         <i>
          may be ambiguous: it could mean the
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inner_product" title="Inner product">
           inner product
          </a>
          or the linear span.
         </i>
         <br/>
         <br/>

         </i>

         </i>

         </i>

         <i>
          S
         </i>
         ).
        </p>
       </td>
       <td>
        <img alt="\left\lang \left( \begin{smallmatrix} 1 \\ 0 \\ 0 \end{smallmatrix} \right), \left( \begin{smallmatrix} 0 \\ 1 \\ 0 \end{smallmatrix} \right), \left( \begin{smallmatrix} 0 \\ 0 \\ 1 \end{smallmatrix} \right) \right\rang = \mathbb{R}^3" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/0/5/5/055d3b7aeb475a70abe821f93593cde9.png"/>
        .

      <tr>
       <td style="padding:0px;">
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:left;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         subgroup
         <a href="/wiki/Generating_set_of_a_group" title="Generating set of a group">
          generated
         </a>

        <img alt=" \langle S \rangle " class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/0/0/c/00c1dc37c488f3467d76cdd967cede4b.png"/>
        means the smallest subgroup of

        <i>
         S
        </i>

         G
        </i>

         S

        .

        <img alt=" \langle g_1, g_2, \ldots, \rangle " class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/a/2/9/a293004cdc51eee0c371fc362e171b2d.png"/>
        is shorthand for
        <img alt=" \langle g_1, g_2, \ldots \rangle " class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/a/2/9/a2933b4afec65765ebdeced8711e6a19.png"/>
        .
       </td>
       <td>
        In
        <a href="/wiki/Dihedral_group_of_order_6" title="Dihedral group of order 6">
         S
         <sub>
          3
         </sub>
        </a>
        ,
        <img alt=" \langle(1 \; 2) \rangle  = \{id,\; (1 \; 2)\} " class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/8/4/6/846d383316e0707600b266722f85242e.png"/>
        and
        <img alt=" \langle (1 \; 2 \; 3) \rangle = \{id, \; (1 \; 2 \; 3),(1 \; 2 \; 3))\} " class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/9/d/a/9da0dc66a866561e8fe0822a595963e8.png"/>
        .
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td style="padding:0px;">
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:left;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         <a href="/wiki/Tuple" title="Tuple">
          tuple
         </a>
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:center;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         tuple;
         <i>
          n
         </i>
         -tuple;
         <br/>
         ordered pair/triple/etc;
         <br/>
         row vector; sequence
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:right;">
         everywhere
        </div>
       </td>
       <td>
        An ordered list (or sequence, or horizontal vector, or row vector) of values.
        <p>
         (
         <i>
          The notation
         </i>
         (
         <i>
          a
         </i>
         ,
         <i>
          b
         </i>
         )
         <i>
          is often used as well.
         </i>
         )
        </p>
       </td>
       <td>
        <img alt=" \langle a, b \rangle " class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/e/c/3/ec35790be969f4af7fd4ad4c2782514f.png"/>
        is an ordered pair (or 2-tuple).
        <p>
         <img alt=" \langle a, b, c \rangle " class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/e/5/4/e54c3ff0e968c3c0502fe9d616512b8e.png"/>
         is an ordered triple (or 3-tuple).
        </p>
        <p>
         <img alt=" \langle \rangle " class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/0/a/a/0aa64b4d34c62565dedba0a3cc00ad56.png"/>
         is the
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Empty_tuple" title="Empty tuple">
          empty tuple
         </a>
         (or 0-tuple).
        </p>
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td align="center" bgcolor="#D0F0D0" rowspan="1">
        <div class="nounderlines" style="font-size:200%;">
         |
         <br/>
         <br/>
         (|)
        </div>
       </td>
       <td align="center" bgcolor="#FFFFFF" rowspan="1">
        <img alt="\langle\ |\ \rangle \!\," class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/d/8/c/d8c2e97f323ec6ab26425a2a0ececbcf.png"/>
        <br/>
        <br/>
        <img alt="(\ |\ ) \!\," class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/5/7/f/57f03b67621df3934218d419fe7570cb.png"/>
       </td>
       <td style="padding:0px;">
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:left;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inner_product" title="Inner product">
          inner product
         </a>
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:center;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         inner product of
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:right;">
         <a href="/wiki/Linear_algebra" title="Linear algebra">
          linear algebra
         </a>
        </div>
       </td>
       <td>
        
        <i>
         u
        </i>
        |
        <i>
         v
        </i>
         means the inner product of
        <i>
         u
        </i>
        and
        <i>
         v
        </i>
        , where
        <i>
         u
        </i>
        and
        <i>
         v
        </i>
        are members of an
        <a href="/wiki/Inner_product_space" title="Inner product space">
         inner product space
        </a>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-m-nielsen-quantum-62_8-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-m-nielsen-quantum-62-8">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          8
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
        (
        <i>
         u
        </i>
        |
        <i>
         v
        </i>
        ) means the same.
        <br/>
        <br/>
        <i>
         Another variant of the notation is
        </i>
        
        <i>
         u
        </i>
        ,
        <i>
         v
        </i>
        
        <i>
         which is described above. For spatial vectors, the
         <a href="/wiki/Dot_product" title="Dot product">
          dot product
         </a>
         notation
        </i>
        ,
        <i>
         x
        </i>
        
        <i>
         y
        </i>
        <i>
         is common. For matrices, the colon notation
        </i>
        <i>
         A
        </i>
        :
        <i>
         B
        </i>
        <i>
         may be used. As
        </i>
        
        <i>
         and
        </i>
        
        <i>
         can be hard to type, the more "keyboard friendly" forms
        </i>
        &lt;
        <i>
         and
        </i>
        &gt;
        <i>
         are sometimes seen. These are avoided in mathematical texts.
        </i>
       </td>
       <td>
       </td>
      </tr>
     </table>

         </a>

       </td>

         <br/>

        </div>

        <i>

        <i>
         y
        </i>
        
        <i>
         x
        </i>

        if X is a uniformly random day of the year P(X is May 25 | X is in May) = 1/31
       </td>

      <tr>
       <td style="padding:0px;">
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:left;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         <a href="/wiki/Restriction_(mathematics)" title="Restriction (mathematics)">
          restriction
         </a>
         <span id="notdivide">
         </span>
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:center;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         restriction of ... to ...;
         <br/>
         restricted to
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:right;">
         <a href="/wiki/Naive_set_theory" title="Naive set theory">

         </a>
        </div>

       </td>
       <td>
        <img alt="\mathrm{S}_n \wr \mathrm{Z}_2" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/2/c/d/2cde17e85b7533e35dea23be21727a45.png"/>
        is isomorphic to the
        <a href="/wiki/Graph_automorphism" title="Graph automorphism">
         automorphism
        </a>
        group of the
        <a href="/wiki/Complete_bipartite_graph" title="Complete bipartite graph">
         complete bipartite graph
        </a>
        on (
        <i>
         n
        </i>
        ,
        <i>
         n
        </i>
        ) vertices.
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td align="center" bgcolor="#D0F0D0" rowspan="1">
        <div class="nounderlines" style="font-size:200%;">
         
         <br/>
         <br/>
         
        </div>
       </td>
       <td align="center" bgcolor="#FFFFFF" rowspan="1">
       </td>
       <td style="padding:0px;">
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:left;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         <a href="/wiki/%E2%86%AF" title="">
          downwards zigzag arrow
         </a>
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:center;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         contradiction; this contradicts that
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:right;">
         everywhere
        </div>
       </td>
       <td>
        Denotes that contradictory statements have been inferred. For clarity, the exact point of contradiction can be appended.
       </td>
       <td>
        x + 4 = x - 3 
        <br/>
        <br/>
        Statement: Every finite, non-empty, ordered set has a largest element. Otherwise, let's assume that
        <img alt="X" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/0/2/1/02129bb861061d1a052c592e2dc6b383.png"/>
        is a finite, non-empty, ordered set with no largest element. Then, for some
        <img alt="x_1 \in X" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/e/8/b/e8b4954f39924636444a3d9f1e90a061.png"/>
        , there exists an
        <img alt="x_2 \in X" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/8/d/0/8d079f0dbb145757e0eca18cf0b56a0e.png"/>
        with
        <img alt="x_1 &lt; x_2" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/e/f/e/efe46c48bf0ef19d5cfb8a4d0860ea0f.png"/>
        , but then there's also an
        <img alt="x_3 \in X" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/6/2/7/62755f720ef65a077ba0c86383530b63.png"/>
        with
        <img alt="x_2 &lt; x_3" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/b/4/3/b438008698afb1753d3939f51d3e92d6.png"/>
        , and so on. Thus,
        <img alt="x_1, x_2, x_3, ..." class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/6/0/e/60ed3591fb7f2ad26a352789c8916bd9.png"/>
        are distinct elements in
        <img alt="X" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/0/2/1/02129bb861061d1a052c592e2dc6b383.png"/>
        . 
        <img alt="X" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/0/2/1/02129bb861061d1a052c592e2dc6b383.png"/>
        is finite.
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td align="center" bgcolor="#D0F0D0" rowspan="2">
        <div class="nounderlines" style="font-size:200%;">
         
         <br/>
         <br/>
         <span class="Unicode">
          
         </span>
        </div>
       </td>
       <td align="center" bgcolor="#FFFFFF" rowspan="2">
        <img alt="\oplus \!\," class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/d/0/b/d0bc33509c009569aa24c01e09265eba.png"/>
        <br/>
        <br/>
        <img alt="\veebar \!\," class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/3/8/0/380c88c727fdc8dd08233d33fe7c4d8c.png"/>
       </td>
       <td style="padding:0px;">
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:left;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         <a href="/wiki/Exclusive_or" title="Exclusive or">
          exclusive or
         </a>
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:center;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         xor
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:right;">
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Propositional_logic" title="Propositional logic">
          propositional logic
         </a>
         ,
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boolean_algebra_(logic)" title="Boolean algebra (logic)">
          Boolean algebra
         </a>
        </div>
       </td>
       <td>
        The statement
        <i>
         A
        </i>
        
        <i>
         B
        </i>
        is true when either A or B, but not both, are true.
        <i>
         A
        </i>
        <span class="Unicode">
         
        </span>
        <i>
         B
        </i>
        means the same.
       </td>
       <td>
        (
        <i>
         A
        </i>
        ) 
        <i>
         A
        </i>
        is always true,
        <i>
         A
        </i>
        
        <i>
         A
        </i>
        is always false.
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td style="padding:0px;">
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:left;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         <a href="/wiki/Direct_sum" title="Direct sum">
          direct sum
         </a>
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:center;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         direct sum of
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:right;">
         <a href="/wiki/Abstract_algebra" title="Abstract algebra">
          abstract algebra
         </a>
        </div>
       </td>
       <td>
        The direct sum is a special way of combining several objects into one general object.
        <br/>
        <br/>
        (
        <i>
         The bun symbol
        </i>
        ,
        <i>
         or the
         <a href="/wiki/Coproduct" title="Coproduct">
          coproduct
         </a>
         symbol
         <span class="Unicode">
          
         </span>
         ,
        </i>
        is used;
        <i>
         <span class="Unicode">
          
         </span>
        </i>
        is only for logic.
        <i>
         )
        </i>
       </td>
       <td>
        Most commonly, for vector spaces
        <i>
         U
        </i>
        ,
        <i>
         V
        </i>
        , and
        <i>
         W
        </i>
        , the following consequence is used:
        <br/>
        <i>
         U
        </i>
        =
        <i>
         V
        </i>
        
        <i>
         W
        </i>
         (
        <i>
         U
        </i>
        =
        <i>
         V
        </i>
        +
        <i>
         W
        </i>
        )  (
        <i>
         V
        </i>
        
        <i>
         W
        </i>
        = {0})
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td align="center" bgcolor="#D0F0D0" rowspan="1">
        <div class="nounderlines" style="font-size:200%;">
        </div>
       </td>
       <td align="center" bgcolor="#FFFFFF" rowspan="1">
        <img alt="{~\wedge\!\!\!\!\!\!\bigcirc~}" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/3/3/2/332ad440b0db38ceb08f77bfc105ee43.png"/>
       </td>
       <td style="padding:0px;">
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:left;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         <a href="/wiki/Kulkarni%E2%80%93Nomizu_product" title="KulkarniNomizu product">
          KulkarniNomizu product
         </a>
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:center;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         KulkarniNomizu product
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:right;">
         <a href="/wiki/Tensor_algebra" title="Tensor algebra">
          tensor algebra
         </a>
        </div>
       </td>
       <td>
        Derived from the
        <a href="/wiki/Tensor_product" title="Tensor product">
         tensor product
        </a>
        of two symmetric type (0,2)
        <a href="/wiki/Tensor" title="Tensor">
         tensors
        </a>
        ; it has the algebraic symmetries of the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Riemann_tensor" title="Riemann tensor">
         Riemann tensor
        </a>
        .
        <img alt="f=g{\,\wedge\!\!\!\!\!\!\bigcirc\,}h" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/5/2/2/52280ca36be2aee2fee913f841094cbb.png"/>
        has components
        <img alt="f_{\alpha\beta\gamma\delta}=g_{\alpha\gamma}h_{\beta\delta}+g_{\beta\delta}h_{\alpha\gamma}-g_{\alpha\delta}h_{\beta\gamma}-g_{\beta\gamma}h_{\alpha\delta}" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/8/c/c/8cce0bc7b3f66c24b306769ef02f9db6.png"/>
        .
       </td>
       <td>
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td align="center" bgcolor="#D0F0D0" rowspan="1">
        <div class="nounderlines" style="font-size:200%;">
         
        </div>
       </td>
       <td align="center" bgcolor="#FFFFFF" rowspan="1">
        <img alt="\Box \!\," class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/6/d/9/6d97a950bc3894e49ef35ed70c1f3f9f.png"/>
       </td>
       <td style="padding:0px;">
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:left;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/D%27Alembertian" title="D'Alembertian">
          D'Alembertian
         </a>
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:center;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         non-Euclidean Laplacian
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:right;">
         <a href="/wiki/Vector_calculus" title="Vector calculus">
          vector calculus
         </a>
        </div>
       </td>
       <td>
        It is the generalisation of the
        <a href="/wiki/Laplace_operator" title="Laplace operator">
         Laplace operator
        </a>
        in the sense that it is the differential operator which is invariant under the isometry group of the underlying space and it reduces to the Laplace operator if restricted to time independent functions.
       </td>
       <td>
        <img alt="\square = \frac{1}{c^2}{\partial^2 \over \partial t^2 } - {\partial^2 \over \partial x^2 } - {\partial^2 \over \partial y^2 } - {\partial^2 \over \partial z^2 } " class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/3/b/c/3bcd036bb08b9dfcece75181dddae655.png"/>
       </td>
      </tr>

        <br/>
        <br/>
        <img alt="\mathbf{N} \!\," class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/a/2/c/a2c1218a4bf60f5297a6713464409ad1.png"/>
       </td>
       <td style="padding:0px;">
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:left;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         <a href="/wiki/Natural_number" title="Natural number">
          natural numbers
         </a>
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:center;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         the (set of) natural numbers
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:right;">
         <a href="/wiki/Number" title="Number">
          numbers
         </a>
        </div>
       </td>
       <td>
        <b>
         N
        </b>
        means either {0, 1, 2, 3, ...} or {1, 2, 3, ...}.
        <br/>
        <br/>
        <i>
         The choice depends on the area of mathematics being studied; e.g.
         <a href="/wiki/Number_theory" title="Number theory">
          number theorists
         </a>
         prefer the latter;
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Analysis_(mathematics)" title="Analysis (mathematics)">
          analysts
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Set_theory" title="Set theory">
          set theorists
         </a>
         and
         <a href="/wiki/Computer_science" title="Computer science">
          computer scientists
         </a>
         prefer the former. To avoid confusion, always check an author's definition of
        </i>
        <b>
         N
        </b>
        .
        <br/>
        <br/>
        <i>
         Set theorists often use the notation
        </i>
        
        <i>
         (for
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Least_infinite_ordinal" title="Least infinite ordinal">
          least infinite ordinal
         </a>
         ) to denote the set of natural numbers (including zero), along with the standard ordering relation
        </i>
        .
       </td>
       <td>
        <span class="Unicode">
         
        </span>
        = {|
        <i>
         a
        </i>
        |:
        <i>
         a
        </i>
        
        <span class="Unicode">
         
        </span>
        }
        <b>
         or
        </b>
        <span class="Unicode">
         
        </span>
        = {|
        <i>
         a
        </i>
        |&gt;0:
        <i>
         a
        </i>
        
        <span class="Unicode">
         
        </span>
        }
       </td>

       <td align="center" bgcolor="#FFFFFF" rowspan="1">
        <img alt="\circ \!\," class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/8/4/7/847fa281bb89dd86aa1feaed408f6a5c.png"/>

         </a>

        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:center;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">

         </a>

       <td>
        For two matrices (or vectors) of the same dimensions
        <img alt=" A, B \in {\mathbb R}^{m \times n} " class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/1/7/9/179955e6e073f7e231455b0b4586771f.png"/>
        the Hadamard product is a matrix of the same dimensions
        <img alt=" A \circ B \in {\mathbb R}^{m \times n} " class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/e/3/b/e3b926abfe562d2458d4ceeadbc9e0f6.png"/>
        with elements given by
        <img alt=" (A \circ B)_{i,j} = (A)_{i,j} \cdot (B)_{i,j}" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/f/b/6/fb6d912053c21f152f78aae3f10b6488.png"/>
        .
        <br/>
        In
        <a href="/wiki/MATLAB" title="MATLAB">
         MATLAB
        </a>
        this operation is expressed by A.*B.

        <img alt="\circ \!\," class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/8/4/7/847fa281bb89dd86aa1feaed408f6a5c.png"/>

        <i>

        </i>

        <a href="/wiki/Infinity" title="Infinity">

        </a>

        <sup>
         4
        </sup>

        <img alt="f(x)=O(g(x))\mbox{ as }x\to\infty\," class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/f/5/1/f510186c8400905d3bcdeafed8793eb2.png"/>

        <span class="Unicode">
         
        </span>
        (Heads)=
        <span class="Unicode">

      <tr>
       <td style="padding:0px;">
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:left;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         <a href="/wiki/Power_set" title="Power set">
          Power set
         </a>
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:center;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         the Power set of
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:right;">
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Powerset" title="Powerset">
          Powerset
         </a>
        </div>
       </td>
       <td>
        Given a set
        <i>
         S
        </i>
        , the power set of
        <i>
         S
        </i>
        is the set of all subsets of the set
        <i>
         S
        </i>
        . The power set of
        <i>
         S
        </i>
        0 is
        <p>
         denoted by P(
         <i>
          S
         </i>
         ).
        </p>
       </td>
       <td>
        The power set P({0, 1, 2}) is the set of all subsets of {0, 1, 2}. Hence,
        <p>
         P({0, 1, 2}) = {, {0}, {1}, {2}, {0, 1}, {0, 2}, {1, 2}, {0, 1, 2. }}
        </p>
       </td>
      </tr>

        <i>
         B
        </i>
        means the set that contains all those elements that
        <i>
         A
        </i>
        and
        <i>
         B
        </i>
        have in common.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-d-goldrei-set-4_5-3">
         <a href="#cite_note-d-goldrei-set-4-5">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          5
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
       </td>
       <td>
        {
        <i>
         x
        </i>
        
        <span class="Unicode">
         
        </span>
        :
        <i>
         x
        </i>
        <sup>
         2
        </sup>
        = 1}
        <span class="Unicode">
         
        </span>
        = {1}
       </td>

       <td align="center" bgcolor="#D0F0D0" rowspan="1">
        <div class="nounderlines" style="font-size:200%;">
         
        </div>
       </td>
       <td align="center" bgcolor="#FFFFFF" rowspan="1">
        <img alt="\or \!\," class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/9/7/4/974392b83dc3446bbd20bdc0df826b42.png"/>
       </td>
       <td style="padding:0px;">
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:left;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         <a href="/wiki/Logical_disjunction" title="Logical disjunction">
          logical disjunction
         </a>
         or
         <b>
          join
         </b>
         in a
         <a href="/wiki/Lattice_(order)" title="Lattice (order)">
          lattice
         </a>
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:center;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         or;
         <br/>
         max;
         <br/>
         join
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:right;">
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Propositional_logic" title="Propositional logic">
          propositional logic
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Lattice_(order)" title="Lattice (order)">
          lattice theory
         </a>
        </div>
       </td>
       <td>
        The statement
        <i>
         A
        </i>
        
        <i>
         B
        </i>
        is true if
        <i>
         A
        </i>
        or
        <i>
         B
        </i>
        (or both) are true; if both are false, the statement is false.
        <br/>
        <br/>
        For functions
        <i>
         A
        </i>
        (x) and
        <i>
         B
        </i>
        (x),
        <i>
         A
        </i>
        (x) 
        <i>
         B
        </i>
        (x) is used to mean max(A(x), B(x)).
       </td>
       <td>
        <i>
         n
        </i>
         4
        <i>
         n
        </i>
         2
        <i>
         n
        </i>
         3 when
        <i>
         n
        </i>
        is a
        <a href="/wiki/Natural_number" title="Natural number">
         natural number
        </a>
        .
       </td>

        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:left;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         <a href="/wiki/Integer" title="Integer">
          integers
         </a>
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:center;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         the (set of) integers
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:right;">
         <a href="/wiki/Number" title="Number">
          numbers
         </a>
        </div>
       </td>
       <td>
        <span class="Unicode">
         
        </span>
        means {..., 3, 2, 1, 0, 1, 2, 3, ...}.
        <p>
         <span class="Unicode">
          
         </span>
         <sup>
          +
         </sup>
         or
         <span class="Unicode">
          
         </span>
         <sup>
          &gt;
         </sup>
         means {1, 2, 3, ...}.
         <br/>
         <span class="Unicode">
          
         </span>
         <sup>
          *
         </sup>
         or
         <span class="Unicode">
          
         </span>
         <sup>
          
         </sup>
         means {0, 1, 2, 3, ...}.
        </p>
       </td>
       <td>
        <span class="Unicode">
         
        </span>
        = {
        <i>
         p
        </i>
        ,
        <i>
         p
        </i>
        :
        <i>
         p
        </i>
        
        <span class="Unicode">
         
        </span>
        {0}}
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td align="center" bgcolor="#D0F0D0" rowspan="2">

        <br/>
        <br/>
        <img alt="\mathbf{Z}_n \!\," class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/6/c/f/6cf99e809356c524faf504ef07e3c33b.png"/>
        <br/>
        <br/>
        <img alt="\mathbf{Z}_p \!\," class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/3/3/e/33e76e9dc5eddfaee68c648151367b3e.png"/>
       </td>
       <td style="padding:0px;">
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:left;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         <a href="/wiki/Modular_arithmetic" title="Modular arithmetic">
          integers mod
          <i>
           n
          </i>
         </a>
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:center;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         the (set of) integers modulo
         <i>
          n
         </i>
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:right;">
         <a href="/wiki/Number" title="Number">
          numbers
         </a>
        </div>
       </td>
       <td>
        <span class="Unicode">
         
        </span>
        <sub>
         <i>
          n
         </i>
        </sub>
        means {[0], [1], [2], ...[
        <i>
         n
        </i>
        1]} with addition and multiplication modulo
        <i>
         n
        </i>
        .
        <br/>
        <br/>
        <i>
         Note that any letter may be used instead of
        </i>
        <i>
         n
        </i>
        ,
        <i>
         such as
        </i>
        <i>
         p
        </i>
        .
        <i>
         To avoid confusion with p-adic numbers, use
        </i>
        <span class="Unicode">
         
        </span>
        /
        <i>
         p
        </i>
        <span class="Unicode">
         
        </span>
        <i>
         or
        </i>
        <span class="Unicode">
         
        </span>
        /(
        <i>
         p
        </i>
        )
        <i>
         instead.
        </i>
       </td>
       <td>
        <span class="Unicode">
         
        </span>
        <sub>
         3
        </sub>
        = {[0], [1], [2]}
       </td>
      </tr>

       <td style="padding:0px;">

        <i>
         
        </i>

        <img alt=" \Delta f = \nabla^2 f = \nabla \cdot \nabla f " class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/b/c/2/bc270359898fccd42052faab9b3bb78d.png"/>

        <i>
         f
        </i>
        (x
        <sub>

        </i>

       <td>

        <img alt="\pi \!\," class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline tex" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/math/6/3/2/6325a65b73ad3051d411effdc6a97e85.png"/>
       </td>
       <td style="padding:0px;">
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:left;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         <a href="/wiki/Pi" title="Pi">
          Pi
         </a>
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:center;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">
         pi;
         <br/>
         3.1415926...;
         <br/>
         227
        </div>
        <div style="padding:2px;text-align:right;">
         <a href="/wiki/Mathematical_constant" title="Mathematical constant">
          mathematical constant
         </a>
        </div>
       </td>
       <td>
        Used in
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_formulae_involving_pi" title="List of formulae involving pi">
         various formulas
        </a>
        involving circles;  is equivalent to the amount of area a circle would take up in a square of equal width with an area of 4 square units, roughly 3.14159. It is also the ratio of the
        <a href="/wiki/Circumference" title="Circumference">
         circumference
        </a>
        to the diameter of a circle.
       </td>
       <td>
        <a href="/wiki/Area" title="Area">
         A
        </a>
        = 
        <a href="/wiki/Radius" title="Radius">
         R
        </a>
        <sup>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Squaring" title="Squaring">
          2
         </a>
        </sup>
        = 314.16  R = 10
       </td>
